    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

              <span id="reviewTextContainer307770762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11996153147569290358"> I wasn't really disappointed about this book. The author doesn't pretend to write literature, so I didn't expect a great deal from it. And yet, I'm surprised, for the novel wasn't as gripping and heart rending as I thought it would be. I did shed a tear or two. But that was it.<br/><br/>'Komt een vrouw bij de dokter' (translated in English as 'Love life') is an account of terminal illness that ends in death. When Carmen is diagnosed with breast cancer, her husband Dan is unable to cope with her illness a</span>
  <span id="freeText11996153147569290358" style="display:none"> I wasn't really disappointed about this book. The author doesn't pretend to write literature, so I didn't expect a great deal from it. And yet, I'm surprised, for the novel wasn't as gripping and heart rending as I thought it would be. I did shed a tear or two. But that was it.<br /><br />'Komt een vrouw bij de dokter' (translated in English as 'Love life') is an account of terminal illness that ends in death. When Carmen is diagnosed with breast cancer, her husband Dan is unable to cope with her illness and the changes it brings to their yuppie family life (they have a daughter, Luna). While Carmen submits to chemotherapy and eventually a mastectomy, hedonistic Dan tries to find solace with his buddies and in several flings. He abandons his wife at crucial times in an attempt to ignore his desperate state of mind. After visiting a 'spiritual' medium, he finally realises that he has to face his wife's imminent death. Eventually of her own accord - and he has to stand by her.<br /><br />Somehow I was unable to perceive this book as a 'novel'. It's just a flimsy story and not even a good one at it. Dan is not the 'anti-hero turning hero' that the press wants him to be. He is wallowing in self-pity all the time, making it seem as if he is the main victim of the cancer. He attributes his escapades to her illness ("it's because of the cancer!"). The transformation of the 'anti-hero' into the 'hero' seems hard to believe. In fact, you don't believe it.<br /><br />Why the tears? Because of some painful scenes. Carmen missing one breast, Dan putting her on the toilet, thinking about their lovemaking in the past and what remains of her body now. But this is as far as it goes. I can't quite imagine why this novel caused such a stir.<br /><br />The novel has some visual flair to it, though. Every chapter starts with some famous lyrics. We get to know Dan a little bit more through his texting his new girlfriend. Kluun also included 'wramples', referring to music samples, but in writing. The yuppie lifestyle of Dan and Carmen is expressed in lengthy and unnecessary detail boxes about the pubs they go and the people they know. <br /><br />All in all, a very mediocre novel. I've already spent way too much time on it simply by reviewing it. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11996153147569290358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer15550917" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15157883249481978796">A penpal recommended this book to me and I eagerly started reading it, because it was so close to my field as a medical professional. It's always interesting to read how patients see their illnesses, and in this case a fatal illness, no matter if the story is real or fiction.<br/><br/>The doctors in the book were pretty awful. No communication skills, no understanding of the patient, just clean and cold professionalism. And in these cases it seemed they weren't even that professional. I hope no doctor lik</span>
  <span id="freeText15157883249481978796" style="display:none">A penpal recommended this book to me and I eagerly started reading it, because it was so close to my field as a medical professional. It's always interesting to read how patients see their illnesses, and in this case a fatal illness, no matter if the story is real or fiction.<br /><br />The doctors in the book were pretty awful. No communication skills, no understanding of the patient, just clean and cold professionalism. And in these cases it seemed they weren't even that professional. I hope no doctor like the ones in the book really exist. I was horrified of the thought!<br /><br />And the me-person in this book, Stijn. What to say about him? I'll just say it: I HATED him. He was such a bastard full of himself! A few examples: <br />* It was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>Carmen[/b:]'s fault that their relationship went down to the drain, according to Stijn. He really "tried" (oh yeah, by cheating her all the time?) to do his best, but Carmen ruined everything. Carmen and her one breast, Carmen and her bad mood, Carmen wanting no sex. Stijn seemed to think Carmen was there for him, and should "put the cancer aside" to fulfil his sexual demands.<br />* Carmen asked Stijn not to cheat her the rest of her life. Is it so damn hard to do as a dying cancer patient asks, considering her "rest of life" is only a couple of months?! Apparently it is, because Stijn continues to cheat her.<br />* In the end of the book Stijn was such "a saint" looking after his wife. He was so proud of himself, being like a hero looking at that dreadful thing that once was his wife. Oh yeah, who's the hero really?! Not Stijn, I'd say. How twisted is it to be so damn proud by sticking to your wife while death is closing on her?!<br /><br />Even if I mostly hated Stijn, at points it did seem that he really did love Carmen, with his own twisted egoistic way. The story was good and I didn't make it through the end with a dry eye.<br /><br />It was also interesting to read about eutanasia. It's not allowed here in Finland, and I think it should be. It's complicated, but it seems The Netherlands have managed to arrange it well. No Dr. Kevorkians here hopefully, but legal eutanasia.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789057591662" href="/book/show/10585767-komt-een-vrouw-bij-de-dokter">review of another edition</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3199336502" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2372746871999620142">I don't really know how to rate this book...CAWPILE tells me its a 3 star book, so I guess that's what I'll give it, although I am sorely tempted to just not give this book a rating at all - it feels like both a 5 and 1 star at the same time, but neither of those feels right either . I hated the main character so much, and I think that was kind of the point, but I also appreciated the very raw look on cancer (I've lost several family members to cancer and had a few family members who had it and </span>
  <span id="freeText2372746871999620142" style="display:none">I don't really know how to rate this book...CAWPILE tells me its a 3 star book, so I guess that's what I'll give it, although I am sorely tempted to just not give this book a rating at all - it feels like both a 5 and 1 star at the same time, but neither of those feels right either . I hated the main character so much, and I think that was kind of the point, but I also appreciated the very raw look on cancer (I've lost several family members to cancer and had a few family members who had it and recovered as well) - it was never an enjoyable read, but I also didn't really expect it to be....I did expect that the main character wouldn't be such an ass...but that's dutch contemporary adult literature for you apparently - apparently main characters are all a**holes here. At it's best the book is just very raw and very honest and even though I wasn't enjoying myself I also never actively wanted to put the book down. I did roll my eyes repeatedly at stijn, I think he's an A-class A**hole and I actively cheered during the scene where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Carmen confronts him and tells him she'd rather divorce him than stay with a guy who cheats on her all the time <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I do appreciate the last 1/3 of this book, after it basically just becomes the story of the MC taking care of his sick wife - him being confronted by all his friends and family, and seeing how everyone copes with it - Carmen really was the highlight of this book and I kinda loved her, she was an unexpected ray of sunshine till the bitter end in the cloudy day that is this book. I'm not sure I'll want to read more by this author, at least nothing that is this brutal - at the end of the day I am glad I read it. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16764667455701456679" style="display:none">Because the main subject of this book was the young woman dying of cancer and having lost one of my closest friends to exactly the same thing this year I somehow feel bad for saying that I didnt like this book at all. <div id="review_36971152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36971152" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1117991-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209204542p2/1117991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36971152?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/1117991-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36971152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer675961186079905287">I'd heard a lot about this book, but still I didn't quite know what to expect. After reading it, I'm still not sure how I feel about it. It's well-written, and the subject will probably touch most readers. In this book, the author tells the story of his wife's struggle against cancer and his own experiences during this time. While he is at times a first-rate bastard and his way of coping is miles and miles away from my own coping mechanisms, it's still interesting to read about it. On the one ha</span>
  <span id="freeText675961186079905287" style="display:none">I'd heard a lot about this book, but still I didn't quite know what to expect. After reading it, I'm still not sure how I feel about it. It's well-written, and the subject will probably touch most readers. In this book, the author tells the story of his wife's struggle against cancer and his own experiences during this time. While he is at times a first-rate bastard and his way of coping is miles and miles away from my own coping mechanisms, it's still interesting to read about it. On the one hand it's shocking, on the other hand it's so incredibly understandable. Who wouldn't want to find ways of forgetting reality, if you were in a situation like this?<br /><br />The ending was very moving. I cried buckets, and still I found myself laughing out loud at certain points. It was very sad, yet strangely uplifting to read about the way Carmen dealt with her impending death. She was an amazing character, and the person she was based on must have been an amazing person. </span>
  <a data-text-id="675961186079905287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3328939626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3328939626" />
    <a title="Sofie De Belder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114954681-sofie-de-belder"><img alt="Sofie De Belder" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3328939626?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofie De Belder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofie De Belder" href="/user/show/114954681-sofie-de-belder">Sofie De Belder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3328939626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8783787325738882084">TOUCHING STORY ABOUT A DIFFICULT TIME<br/><br/>A few weeks ago, I read the book ‘Komt een vrouw bij de dokter’ from Kluun. This beautiful story will drag you into the life of Stijn and Carmen. They are a happy couple and have a one year old daughter, Luna. <br/>One day they are told that Carmen has breast cancer. She undergoes a heavy procedure with a lot of pain. Stijn is always there for Carmen but unfortunately he also keeps some secrets. Stijn often cheats on Carmen without her knowing it. However, he alwa</span>
  <span id="freeText8783787325738882084" style="display:none">TOUCHING STORY ABOUT A DIFFICULT TIME<br /><br />A few weeks ago, I read the book ‘Komt een vrouw bij de dokter’ from Kluun. This beautiful story will drag you into the life of Stijn and Carmen. They are a happy couple and have a one year old daughter, Luna. <br />One day they are told that Carmen has breast cancer. She undergoes a heavy procedure with a lot of pain. Stijn is always there for Carmen but unfortunately he also keeps some secrets. Stijn often cheats on Carmen without her knowing it. However, he always continues to support her during all those difficult years. <br />A touching quote from the book is: “Ik heb kanker, en als je dit leest ben ik er niet meer” (Kluun, 2014, p. 181), which means: "I have cancer, and when you read this, I'm no longer here”. That is what Carmen wrote in a book for Luna, when she thought she was about to die.<br /><br />Stijn, Carmen and Roos are the main characters in the book. <br />Stijn tells the story from his perspective. He has already cheated on Carmen with about 30 women. He doesn't have an easy life, but in spite of everything he continues to support Carmen. I don't approve at all of what Stijn is doing while Carmen has cancer. However, if you read the book, you somehow feel sorry for him.<br />Carmen is Stijn’s wife. When she was told she had cancer, her world collapsed. I feel very sorry for her, she had some difficult years.<br />Roos is Stijn's mistress. They get to know each other during Carnival. I don't like her character. She knows that Stijn is cheating but still allows him into her life.<br /><br />The author didn't just simply write this story. It is based on his life … He really did cheat on his wife when she had cancer. When I knew this, the book got even more touching. It's about how weak he was when his wife needed him. Of course, he now regrets all this cheating, but he wrote his feelings down very well in the book.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this story. Kluun's writing style is very accessible. He writes straight from the heart, of course also because he experienced the story himself. He wrote the story in such a way that you have to feel sorry for him, which is almost impossible for someone who is cheating. My favourite part of the book was the end. If you want to know what happens then, you will have to read it yourself ... <br />I think the book was complete. There were no missing parts and the ending was perfect. It was incredibly well structured and it's now one of my favourite books.<br /><br />Overall, I think 'Komt een vrouw bij de dokter’ is a real recommendation. You are dragged into a sad but very lovely story. That's why it deserves 5 stars!<br /><br />Kluun, (2014). Komt een vrouw bij de dokter. Amsterdam: Rainbow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8783787325738882084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Summers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Summers" href="/user/show/79041655-jennifer-summers">Jennifer Summers</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781466834026" href="/book/show/16283488-love-life">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2803406299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9891540601340032896">After the first 20% I was ready to declare this the worst book I'd ever read... I found the lead character/author AWFUL. A completely self obsessed misogynist, who appears to think sticking a quote at the start of every chapter counts as him being deep or literary. The way he talks about his work in advertising is cringeworthy and he has absolutely no other point of reference to anything other than Ajax football team. Whats worse, he cheats and lies to his dying wife constantly. For me this init</span>
  <span id="freeText9891540601340032896" style="display:none">After the first 20% I was ready to declare this the worst book I'd ever read... I found the lead character/author AWFUL. A completely self obsessed misogynist, who appears to think sticking a quote at the start of every chapter counts as him being deep or literary. The way he talks about his work in advertising is cringeworthy and he has absolutely no other point of reference to anything other than Ajax football team. Whats worse, he cheats and lies to his dying wife constantly. For me this initially meant that any passages in which he spoke of his love for his wife just felt completely inauthentic and frustrating to read. <br /><br />However, as I got deeper into the book I do have to admit it started to strike a chord with me. The subject is so sad it is difficult not to get drawn into the story emotionally, and I did find myself empathising with the lead more and more. It's portrayal not only of the physical effect of cancer, but a couple's emotionally complex responses to such tragedy, provided me with insight into a very real life scenario that I was previously unfamiliar with.<br /><br />I stand by my initial reaction that the lead male is a bit of an idiot, but the book is a definite page turner.<br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1723885163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer17728903934037336339">(contains spoilers)<br/><br/><br/><br/>It had the potential to be a good book. Very realistic and emotional. However the male MC ruined the plot. I couldn't understand how in the end the author wanted to show us Dan's deep love for his dying wife when he cheated on her so many times and not just when the tough times started. The emotional struggles of the couple through and dynamics were powerful but still the unfaithful MC didn't help me feel it was all real. Definitely ended up in tears though. </span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F5cYRNkbsNZDU3ZMVjxKzX6pz8bV1Tq9UPd0mrW5wr4xjEkl74IHFVB7ThN3yauuf5+FuKNk5pjXTiX3eFrn+g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Husygruo+hp4N7FryBh8QwVSVcBl2cL7H66mkEi4Mjo48GPjjTFN2WsfiTTp7Z0gBGQfvhNoHt6YF/f9hVsXfg==')})
  }
//]]>

Jörgen Hofmeester is vader van twee dochters en werkzaam voor een gerenommeerd bedrijf. Dankzij een uitgekiend financieel beleid woont hij op stand: bandeloosheid leidt tot rampen. Stilstand is voor Hofmeester de voorwaarde voor liefde en geluk. Loom houdt hij van zijn dochters. Dat zijn echtgenote hem ingeruild heeft voor een jeugdliefde op een woonboot en dat een gedeelte van zijn vermogen is verdwenen door malversaties van merkwaardige groeperingen die de wereldeconomie beheersen, het deert hem niet. Zolang hij maar van zijn kinderen mag houden. Maar op een avond staat zijn echtgenote weer voor de deur. En dan doet een man zijn intrede in het leven van Jörgen Hofmeester, een man die als twee druppels water op Mohammed Atta lijkt.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12378791036454027971\" href=\"#\" Het luidt de val van de onaantastbare Willem Holleeder in.\nWat weinigen wisten, is dat Willem Holleeder zijn familie dertig jaar lang terroriseerde, afperste en bedreigde, precies zoals zijn alcoholistische vader – werknemer bij Heineken – de familie jarenlang had overheerst en mishandeld. Kinderen, vrouwen, aangetrouwde familie, tot aan moeder Stien toe: niemand ontkwam aan hun despotische gedrag.\nJudas speelt zich af tussen 2012 en het heden, en is doorspekt met flashbacks naar spraakmakende gebeurtenissen in het verleden. Het is een verbijsterende familiekroniek waarin Astrid Holleeder een onthutsend portret schetst van een gezin dat sinds 1983 – het jaar van de Heineken-ontvoering – alleen nog maar een achternaam heeft: Holleeder. In dit unieke boek vertelt zij op indringende wijze over de impact van de ontvoering op alle familieleden, de verwijdering tussen de bloedgabbers Willem Holleeder en Cor van Hout (die in 2003 om het leven kwam), de bedreiging van Peter R. de Vries, liquidaties en afpersingen in het criminele milieu. Ook spreekt ze vrijuit over haar jeugd en haar moeder, de kinderen, haar ex-partners, haar werk als advocate en haar dubbelrol als consigliere van haar broer.\nDoor zich als vertrouweling op te stellen kon Astrid dicht in de nabijheid van haar broer verkeren, en hun gesprekken in het geheim opnemen, met maar één doel: hem levenslang geven.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6808136855656458979\" <span id="freeTextContainer8454745980958153013">See also the author profile for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5840966.Ray_Kluun' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ray Kluun</a> . All his books were first published (in Dutch) under the author name Kluun. Many translations are published under the name of "Ray Kluun".<br/><br/>After Kluun's wife died of cancer, he started to write down his experiences in his first book "Komt een vrouw bij de dokter" ("A woman visited her doctor" - translated into English as "Love life") which wasn't well rece</span>
  <span id="freeText8454745980958153013" style="display:none">See also the author profile for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5840966.Ray_Kluun" rel="nofollow noopener">Ray Kluun</a> . All his books were first published (in Dutch) under the author name Kluun. Many translations are published under the name of "Ray Kluun".<br /><br />After Kluun's wife died of cancer, he started to write down his experiences in his first book "Komt een vrouw bij de dokter" ("A woman visited her doctor" - translated into English as "Love life") which wasn't well received by the critics, but sold 500.000 copies in the Netherlands. He also wrote a sequel called "The widow".<br /><br />"The widow" was followed up by a book called "Help I inpregnated my wife" which deals with the experiences of a man during the pregnancy of his wife. <br /><br />He wrote two other book after that, one of which was given away for free with the purchase of a sixpack of beer. <br /><br />Kluun is also the founder of an internet community for ugly people, which he founded as a parody of an internet dating site which only accepted "good looking" people.</span>
